     External links\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </li>\n       </ul>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Origins">\n        Origins\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The word\n       <i>\n        enthalpy\n       </i>\n       stems from the\n       <a href="/wiki/Ancient_Greek" title="Ancient Greek">\n        Ancient Greek\n       </a>\n       verb\n       <i>\n        enthalpein\n       </i>\n       (\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        \xe1\xbc\x90\xce\xbd\xce\xb8\xce\xac\xce\xbb\xcf\x80\xce\xb5\xce\xb9\xce\xbd\n       </span>\n       ), which means "to warm in".\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-4">\n        <a href="#cite_note-4">\n         [4]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       It combines the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Classical_Greek_language" title="Classical Greek language">\n        Classical Greek\n       </a>\n       prefix\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%E1%BC%90%CE%BD" title="wikt:\xe1\xbc\x90\xce\xbd">\n         \xe1\xbc\x90\xce\xbd-\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <i>\n        en-\n       </i>\n       , meaning "to put into", and the verb\n       <span lang="grc" xml:lang="grc">\n        <a class="extiw" href="https://en.wiktionary.org/wiki/%CE%B8%CE%AC%CE%BB%CF%80%CF%89" title="wikt:\xce\xb8\xce\xac\xce\xbb\xcf\x80\xcf\x89">\n         \xce\xb8\xce\xac\xce\xbb\xcf\x80\xce\xb5\xce\xb9\xce\xbd\n        </a>\n       </span>\n       <i>\n        thalpein\n       </i>\n       , meaning "to heat". The word\n       <i>\n        enthalpy\n       </i>\n       is often incorrectly attributed to\n       <a href="/wiki/Beno%C3%AEt_Paul_%C3%89mile_Clapeyron" title="Beno\xc3\xaet Paul \xc3\x89mile Clapeyron">\n        Beno\xc3\xaet Paul \xc3\x89mile Clapeyron\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Rudolf_Clausius" title="Rudolf Clausius">\n        Rudolf Clausius\n       </a>\n       through the 1850 publication of their\n       <a href="/wiki/Clausius%E2%80%93Clapeyron_relation" title="Clausius\xe2\x80\x93Clapeyron relation">\n        Clausius\xe2\x80\x93Clapeyron relation\n       </a>\n       . This misconception was popularized by the 1927 publication of\n       <i>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy%E2%80%93entropy_chart" title="Enthalpy\xe2\x80\x93entropy chart">\n         The Mollier Steam Tables and Diagrams\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       . However, neither the concept, the word, nor the symbol for enthalpy existed until well after Clapeyron\'s death.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The earliest writings to contain the concept of enthalpy did not appear until 1875,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5">\n        <a href="#cite_note-5">\n         [5]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       when\n       <a href="/wiki/Josiah_Willard_Gibbs" title="Josiah Willard Gibbs">\n        Josiah Willard Gibbs\n       </a>\n       introduced "a heat function for constant pressure". However, Gibbs did not use the word "enthalpy" in his writings.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6">\n        <a href="#cite_note-6">\n         [note 1]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The actual word first appears in the scientific literature in a 1909 publication by J. P. Dalton. According to that publication,\n       <a href="/wiki/Heike_Kamerlingh_Onnes" title="Heike Kamerlingh Onnes">\n        Heike Kamerlingh Onnes\n       </a>\n       actually coined the word.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7">\n        <a href="#cite_note-7">\n         [6]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Over the years, scientists used many different symbols to denote enthalpy. In 1922 Alfred W. Porter proposed the symbol "\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       " as a standard,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howard_8-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Howard-8">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       thus finalizing the terminology still in use today.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In the past, enthalpy was sometimes called\n       <i>\n        heat content\n       </i>\n       .\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9">\n        <a href="#cite_note-9">\n         [8]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Howard_8-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Howard-8">\n         [7]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10">\n        <a href="#cite_note-10">\n         [9]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       The fact that the change in enthalpy \xce\x94H equals the heat absorbed in processes at constant pressure is the reason for this name.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11">\n        <a href="#cite_note-11">\n         [10]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       However this equality is not true in general (when the pressure varies), so that the term\n       <i>\n        heat content\n       </i>\n       is considered misleading\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12">\n        <a href="#cite_note-12">\n         [11]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       and is now\n       <a href="/wiki/Deprecation" title="Deprecation">\n        deprecated\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Formal_definition">\n        Formal definition\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Formal definition">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The enthalpy of a homogeneous system is defined as\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guggenheim_13-0">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Guggenheim-13">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14">\n        <a href="#cite_note-14">\n         [13]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               U\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle H=U+pV,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle H=U+pV,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/c514fbfcfb3cccea0d47af1efe44d27a3b06d065" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:13.462ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         H\n        </i>\n        is the enthalpy of the system,\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         U\n        </i>\n        is the\n        <a href="/wiki/Internal_energy" title="Internal energy">\n         internal energy\n        </a>\n        of the system,\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        is the\n        <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">\n         pressure\n        </a>\n        of the system,\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         V\n        </i>\n        is the\n        <a href="/wiki/Volume_(thermodynamics)" title="Volume (thermodynamics)">\n         volume\n        </a>\n        of the system.\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Enthalpy is an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Extensive_property" title="Extensive property">\n        extensive property\n       </a>\n       . This means that, for homogeneous systems, the enthalpy is proportional to the size of the system. It is convenient to introduce the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Specific_enthalpy" title="Specific enthalpy">\n        specific enthalpy\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       =\n       <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n         <i>\n          H\n         </i>\n        </span>\n        <span class="visualhide">\n         /\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n         <i>\n          m\n         </i>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       , where\n       <i>\n        m\n       </i>\n       is the mass of the system, or the molar enthalpy\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        m\n       </sub>\n       =\n       <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n         <i>\n          H\n         </i>\n        </span>\n        <span class="visualhide">\n         /\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n         <i>\n          n\n         </i>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       , where\n       <i>\n        n\n       </i>\n       is the number of moles (\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        m\n       </sub>\n       are\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Intensive_properties" title="Intensive properties">\n        intensive properties\n       </a>\n       ). For inhomogeneous systems the enthalpy is the sum of the enthalpies of the composing subsystems:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <munder>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x91\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x91 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 k\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </munder>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                H\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 k\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle H=\\sum _{k}H_{k},}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle H=\\sum _{k}H_{k},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/413a53dcd509e77d375d9a97abec0be638534d3e" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:12.631ex; height:5.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where the label\n       <i>\n        k\n       </i>\n       refers to the various subsystems. In case of continuously varying\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       or composition, the summation becomes an integral:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\xab\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\xab -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xcf\x81\n               <!-- \xcf\x81 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               h\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle H=\\int \\rho h\\,dV,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle H=\\int \\rho h\\,dV,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/4f7133e4638ba53bc2495e8ef2b3f20ba9a8e8cf" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:14.404ex; height:5.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where\n       <i>\n        \xcf\x81\n       </i>\n       is the density.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The enthalpy of homogeneous systems can be viewed as function\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       (\n       <i>\n        S\n       </i>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       ) of the entropy\n       <i>\n        S\n       </i>\n       and the pressure\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       , and a differential relation for it can be derived as follows. We start from the\n       <a href="/wiki/First_law_of_thermodynamics" title="First law of thermodynamics">\n        first law of thermodynamics\n       </a>\n       for closed systems for an infinitesimal process:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               U\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               Q\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               W\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dU=\\delta Q-\\delta W.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dU=\\delta Q-\\delta W.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/24a3f403ec5d284eda79a351e8d62fb49979fa9e" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.049ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Here,\n       <i>\n        \xce\xb4Q\n       </i>\n       is a small amount of heat added to the system, and\n       <i>\n        \xce\xb4W\n       </i>\n       a small amount of work performed by the system. In a homogeneous system only reversible processes can take place, so the\n       <a href="/wiki/Second_law_of_thermodynamics" title="Second law of thermodynamics">\n        second law of thermodynamics\n       </a>\n       gives\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         \xce\xb4Q\n        </i>\n        =\n        <i>\n         T\xe2\x80\x89dS\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       , with\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Absolute_temperature" title="Absolute temperature">\n        absolute temperature\n       </a>\n       of the system. Furthermore, if only\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       work is done,\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         \xce\xb4W\n        </i>\n        =\n        <i>\n         p\xe2\x80\x89dV\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       . As a result,\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               U\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               S\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dU=T\\,dS-p\\,dV.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dU=T\\,dS-p\\,dV.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/1ef742fd11c96cc41357e3b6a3a60334db32b5e4" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:18.997ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Adding\n       <i>\n        d\n       </i>\n       (\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       ) to both sides of this expression gives\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               U\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               S\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dU+d(pV)=T\\,dS-p\\,dV+d(pV),}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dU+d(pV)=T\\,dS-p\\,dV+d(pV),}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/9738fd98a4e8110fee88d4c6286008e76c2620ad" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:36.767ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       or\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               U\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               S\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle d(U+pV)=T\\,dS+V\\,dp.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle d(U+pV)=T\\,dS+V\\,dp.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/5bb74adcf1f8403e6421e347d58f25c7982673b5" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:26.656ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       So\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               S\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               S\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dH(S,p)=T\\,dS+V\\,dp.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dH(S,p)=T\\,dS+V\\,dp.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/60e3a808397f9827b72e439abb2d6d13beec1c74" style="vertical-align: -0.838ex; width:24.842ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Other_expressions">\n        Other expressions\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Other expressions">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The above expression of\n       <i>\n        dH\n       </i>\n       in terms of entropy and pressure may be unfamiliar to some readers. However, there are expressions in terms of more familiar variables such as temperature and pressure:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Guggenheim_13-1">\n        <a href="#cite_note-Guggenheim-13">\n         [12]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        :88\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15">\n        <a href="#cite_note-15">\n         [14]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                C\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 p\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mn>\n               1\n              </mn>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb1\n               <!-- \xce\xb1 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dH=C_{p}\\,dT+V(1-\\alpha T)\\,dp.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dH=C_{p}\\,dT+V(1-\\alpha T)\\,dp.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8249df68125cf622a2ea12120ec648ed2eb99f4f" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:29.506ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Here\n       <i>\n        C\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n       </sub>\n       is the heat capacity at constant pressure and\n       <i>\n        \xce\xb1\n       </i>\n       is the coefficient of (cubic) thermal expansion:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb1\n               <!-- \xce\xb1 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mfrac>\n                <mn>\n                 1\n                </mn>\n                <mi>\n                 V\n                </mi>\n               </mfrac>\n              </mrow>\n              <msub>\n               <mrow>\n                <mo>\n                 (\n                </mo>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mfrac>\n                  <mrow>\n                   <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                    \xe2\x88\x82\n                    <!-- \xe2\x88\x82 -->\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi>\n                    V\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                  <mrow>\n                   <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                    \xe2\x88\x82\n                    <!-- \xe2\x88\x82 -->\n                   </mi>\n                   <mi>\n                    T\n                   </mi>\n                  </mrow>\n                 </mfrac>\n                </mrow>\n                <mo>\n                 )\n                </mo>\n               </mrow>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 p\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\alpha ={\\frac {1}{V}}\\left({\\frac {\\partial V}{\\partial T}}\\right)_{p}.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle \\alpha ={\\frac {1}{V}}\\left({\\frac {\\partial V}{\\partial T}}\\right)_{p}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/a2aff8db160ea8d3e9d900bfd5462ec78e0f4a87" style="vertical-align: -2.838ex; width:16.369ex; height:6.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       With this expression one can, in principle, determine the enthalpy if\n       <i>\n        C\n        <sub>\n         p\n        </sub>\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        V\n       </i>\n       are known as functions of\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       and\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Note that for an\n       <a href="/wiki/Ideal_gas" title="Ideal gas">\n        ideal gas\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        \xce\xb1T\n       </i>\n       =\xc2\xa01,\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16">\n        <a href="#cite_note-16">\n         [note 2]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       so that\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                C\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 p\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dH=C_{p}\\,dT.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dH=C_{p}\\,dT.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/b7057089b9281f183796ba3fea0613f4e0e1948b" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:13.066ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       In a more general form, the first law describes the internal energy with additional terms involving the\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemical_potential" title="Chemical potential">\n        chemical potential\n       </a>\n       and the number of particles of various types. The differential statement for\n       <i>\n        dH\n       </i>\n       then becomes\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               T\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               S\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <munder>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x91\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x91 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </munder>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                \xce\xbc\n                <!-- \xce\xbc -->\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                N\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 i\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dH=T\\,dS+V\\,dp+\\sum _{i}\\mu _{i}\\,dN_{i},}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dH=T\\,dS+V\\,dp+\\sum _{i}\\mu _{i}\\,dN_{i},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/8a8e570f8957418ae3b62b5ba131e11757b144dc" style="vertical-align: -3.005ex; width:32.398ex; height:5.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where\n       <i>\n        \xce\xbc\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <i>\n         i\n        </i>\n       </sub>\n       is the chemical potential per particle for an\n       <i>\n        i\n       </i>\n       -type particle, and\n       <i>\n        N\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <i>\n         i\n        </i>\n       </sub>\n       is the number of such particles. The last term can also be written as\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         \xce\xbc\n         <sub>\n          i\n         </sub>\n        </i>\n        <i>\n         dn\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         <i>\n          i\n         </i>\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       (with\n       <i>\n        dn\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <i>\n         i\n        </i>\n       </sub>\n       the number of moles of component\n       <i>\n        i\n       </i>\n       added to the system and, in this case,\n       <i>\n        \xce\xbc\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <i>\n         i\n        </i>\n       </sub>\n       the molar chemical potential) or as\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         \xce\xbc\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         <i>\n          i\n         </i>\n        </sub>\n        <i>\n         dm\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         <i>\n          i\n         </i>\n        </sub>\n       </span>\n       (with\n       <i>\n        dm\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <i>\n         i\n        </i>\n       </sub>\n       the mass of component\n       <i>\n        i\n       </i>\n       added to the system and, in this case,\n       <i>\n        \xce\xbc\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <i>\n         i\n        </i>\n       </sub>\n       the specific chemical potential).\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Physical_interpretation">\n        Physical interpretation\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Physical interpretation">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       The\n       <i>\n        U\n       </i>\n       term can be interpreted as the energy required to create the system, and the\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       term as the energy that would be required to "make room" for the system if the pressure of the environment remained constant. When a system, for example,\n       <i>\n        n\n       </i>\n       <a href="/wiki/Mole_(unit)" title="Mole (unit)">\n        moles\n       </a>\n       of a gas of\n       <a href="/wiki/Volume_(thermodynamics)" title="Volume (thermodynamics)">\n        volume\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        V\n       </i>\n       at\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">\n        pressure\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">\n        temperature\n       </a>\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       , is created or brought to its present state from\n       <a href="/wiki/Absolute_zero" title="Absolute zero">\n        absolute zero\n       </a>\n       , energy must be supplied equal to its internal energy\n       <i>\n        U\n       </i>\n       plus\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       , where\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       is the\n       <a href="/wiki/Work_(physics)" title="Work (physics)">\n        work\n       </a>\n       done in pushing against the ambient (atmospheric) pressure.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       In basic\n       <a href="/wiki/Physics" title="Physics">\n        physics\n       </a>\n       and\n       <a href="/wiki/Statistical_mechanics" title="Statistical mechanics">\n        statistical mechanics\n       </a>\n       it may be more interesting to study the internal properties of the system and therefore the internal energy is used.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17">\n        <a href="#cite_note-17">\n         [15]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18">\n        <a href="#cite_note-18">\n         [16]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n       In basic\n       <a href="/wiki/Chemistry" title="Chemistry">\n        chemistry\n       </a>\n       , experiments are often conducted at constant\n       <a href="/wiki/Atmospheric_pressure" title="Atmospheric pressure">\n        atmospheric pressure\n       </a>\n       , and the pressure-volume work represents an energy exchange with the atmosphere that cannot be accessed or controlled, so that \xce\x94\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       is the expression chosen for the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Heat_of_reaction" title="Heat of reaction">\n        heat of reaction\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For a\n       <a href="/wiki/Heat_engine" title="Heat engine">\n        heat engine\n       </a>\n       a change in its internal energy is the difference between the heat input and the\n       <a href="/wiki/Work_(thermodynamics)#Pressure-volume_work" title="Work (thermodynamics)">\n        pressure-volume work\n       </a>\n       done by the working substance while a change in its enthalpy is the difference between the heat input and the work done by the engine:\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19">\n        <a href="#cite_note-19">\n         [17]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               Q\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               W\n              </mi>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dH=\\delta Q-\\delta W}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dH=\\delta Q-\\delta W}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/927be751eb63d061213f0edd29131286b4231283" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:15.673ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where the work W done by the engine is:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               W\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\xae\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle W=-\\oint Vdp}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle W=-\\oint Vdp}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/e05672cfd38150d153f88deaa5a850dd65209510" style="vertical-align: -2.338ex; width:14.555ex; height:5.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Relationship_to_heat">\n        Relationship to heat\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Relationship to heat">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In order to discuss the relation between the enthalpy increase and heat supply, we return to the first law for closed systems:\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         dU\n        </i>\n        =\n        <i>\n         \xce\xb4Q\n        </i>\n        \xe2\x88\x92\n        <i>\n         \xce\xb4W\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       . We apply it to the special case with a uniform pressure at the surface. In this case the work term can be split into two contributions, the so-called\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       work, given by\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         p\xe2\x80\x89dV\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       (where here\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       is the pressure at the surface,\n       <i>\n        dV\n       </i>\n       is the increase of the volume of the system) and all other types of work\n       <i>\n        \xce\xb4W\xe2\x80\xb2\n       </i>\n       , such as by a shaft or by electromagnetic interaction. So we write\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         \xce\xb4W\n        </i>\n        =\n        <i>\n         p\xe2\x80\x89dV\n        </i>\n        +\n        <i>\n         \xce\xb4W\xe2\x80\xb2\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       . In this case the first law reads:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               U\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               Q\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                W\n               </mi>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x80\xb2\n               </mo>\n              </msup>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dU=\\delta Q-p\\,dV-\\delta W\',}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dU=\\delta Q-p\\,dV-\\delta W\',}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/130b005b6859579a3c26f718c2a22b217a7bf4c4" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:24.256ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       or\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               Q\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               V\n              </mi>\n              <mspace width="thinmathspace">\n              </mspace>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               p\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <msup>\n               <mi>\n                W\n               </mi>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x80\xb2\n               </mo>\n              </msup>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dH=\\delta Q+V\\,dp-\\delta W\'.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dH=\\delta Q+V\\,dp-\\delta W\'.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/63dff4546a797e2919b25100eae3cabbdb51d686" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:24.537ex; height:2.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       From this relation we see that the increase in enthalpy of a system is equal to the added\n       <a href="/wiki/Heat" title="Heat">\n        heat\n       </a>\n       :\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               Q\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dH=\\delta Q,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dH=\\delta Q,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/968059d03ab392158165cd7425dd770c9662760c" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:9.974ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       provided that the system is under\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Isobaric_system" title="Isobaric system">\n        constant pressure\n       </a>\n       (\n       <i>\n        dp\n       </i>\n       =\xc2\xa00) and that the only work done by the system is expansion work (\n       <i>\n        \xce\xb4W\'\n       </i>\n       =\xc2\xa00).\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20">\n        <a href="#cite_note-20">\n         [18]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Applications">\n        Applications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Applications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <p>\n       In thermodynamics, one can calculate enthalpy by determining the requirements for creating a system from "nothingness"; the mechanical work required,\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       , differs based upon the conditions that obtain during the creation of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Thermodynamic_system" title="Thermodynamic system">\n        thermodynamic system\n       </a>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       <a href="/wiki/Energy" title="Energy">\n        Energy\n       </a>\n       must be supplied to remove particles from the surroundings to make space for the creation of the system, assuming that the pressure\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       remains constant; this is the\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       term. The supplied energy must also provide the change in internal energy,\n       <i>\n        U\n       </i>\n       , which includes\n       <a href="/wiki/Activation_energy" title="Activation energy">\n        activation energies\n       </a>\n       , ionization energies, mixing energies, vaporization energies, chemical bond energies, and so forth. Together, these constitute the change in the enthalpy\n       <i>\n        U\n       </i>\n       +\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       . For systems at constant pressure, with no external work done other than the\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       work, the change in enthalpy is the heat received by the system.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For a simple system, with a constant number of particles, the difference in enthalpy is the maximum amount of thermal energy derivable from a thermodynamic process in which the pressure is held constant.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21">\n        <a href="#cite_note-21">\n         [19]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Heat_of_reaction">\n        Heat of reaction\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Heat of reaction">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Standard_enthalpy_of_reaction" title="Standard enthalpy of reaction">\n        Standard enthalpy of reaction\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The total enthalpy of a system cannot be measured directly, the\n       <i>\n        enthalpy change\n       </i>\n       of a\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/System_(thermodynamics)" title="System (thermodynamics)">\n        system\n       </a>\n       is measured instead. Enthalpy change is defined by the following equation:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi mathvariant="normal">\n               \xce\x94\n               <!-- \xce\x94 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               H\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                H\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  f\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                H\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="normal">\n                  i\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle \\Delta H=H_{\\mathrm {f} }-H_{\\mathrm {i} },}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle \\Delta H=H_{\\mathrm {f} }-H_{\\mathrm {i} },}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/472c7be7d6ba8dadd8b2e3ca368944bdf3a60651" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.069ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        \xce\x94\n        <i>\n         H\n        </i>\n        is the "enthalpy change",\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         H\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         f\n        </sub>\n        is the final enthalpy of the system (in a chemical reaction, the enthalpy of the products),\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <i>\n         H\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         i\n        </sub>\n        is the initial enthalpy of the system (in a chemical reaction, the enthalpy of the reactants).\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       For an\n       <a href="/wiki/Exothermic_reaction" title="Exothermic reaction">\n        exothermic reaction\n       </a>\n       at constant\n       <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">\n        pressure\n       </a>\n       , the system\'s change in enthalpy equals the energy released in the reaction, including the energy retained in the system and lost through expansion against its surroundings. In a similar manner, for an\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Endothermic" title="Endothermic">\n        endothermic\n       </a>\n       reaction, the system\'s change in enthalpy is equal to the energy\n       <i>\n        absorbed\n       </i>\n       in the reaction, including the energy\n       <i>\n        lost by\n       </i>\n       the system and\n       <i>\n        gained\n       </i>\n       from compression from its surroundings. A relatively easy way to determine whether or not a reaction is exothermic or endothermic is to determine the sign of \xce\x94\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       . If \xce\x94\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       is positive, the reaction is endothermic, that is heat is absorbed by the system due to the products of the reaction having a greater enthalpy than the reactants. On the other hand, if \xce\x94\n       <i>\n        H\n       </i>\n       is negative, the reaction is exothermic, that is the overall decrease in enthalpy is achieved by the generation of heat.\n       <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22">\n        <a href="#cite_note-22">\n         [20]\n        </a>\n       </sup>\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Specific_enthalpy">\n        Specific enthalpy\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Specific enthalpy">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The specific enthalpy of a uniform system is defined as\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       =\n       <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n         <i>\n          H\n         </i>\n        </span>\n        <span class="visualhide">\n         /\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n         <i>\n          m\n         </i>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       where\n       <i>\n        m\n       </i>\n       is the mass of the system. The\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/SI_unit" title="SI unit">\n        SI unit\n       </a>\n       for specific enthalpy is joule per kilogram. It can be expressed in other specific quantities by\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        =\n        <i>\n         u\n        </i>\n        +\n        <i>\n         pv\n        </i>\n       </span>\n       , where\n       <i>\n        u\n       </i>\n       is the specific\n       <a href="/wiki/Internal_energy" title="Internal energy">\n        internal energy\n       </a>\n       ,\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       is the pressure, and\n       <i>\n        v\n       </i>\n       is specific volume, which is equal to\n       <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n         1\n        </span>\n        <span class="visualhide">\n         /\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n         <i>\n          \xcf\x81\n         </i>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       , where\n       <i>\n        \xcf\x81\n       </i>\n       is the density.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Enthalpy_changes">\n        Enthalpy changes\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Enthalpy changes">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       An enthalpy change describes the change in enthalpy observed in the constituents of a thermodynamic system when undergoing a transformation or chemical reaction. It is the difference between the enthalpy after the process has completed, i.e. the enthalpy of the\n       <a href="/wiki/Product_(chemistry)" title="Product (chemistry)">\n        products\n       </a>\n       , and the initial enthalpy of the system, i.e. the reactants. These processes are reversible\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="(March 2015)">\n           why?\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       and the enthalpy for the reverse process is the negative value of the forward change.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       A common standard enthalpy change is the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_formation" title="Enthalpy of formation">\n        enthalpy of formation\n       </a>\n       , which has been determined for a large number of substances. Enthalpy changes are routinely measured and compiled in chemical and physical reference works, such as the\n       <a href="/wiki/CRC_Handbook_of_Chemistry_and_Physics" title="CRC Handbook of Chemistry and Physics">\n        CRC Handbook of Chemistry and Physics\n       </a>\n       . The following is a selection of enthalpy changes commonly recognized in thermodynamics.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       When used in these recognized terms the qualifier\n       <i>\n        change\n       </i>\n       is usually dropped and the property is simply termed\n       <i>\n        enthalpy of \'process\'\n       </i>\n       . Since these properties are often used as reference values it is very common to quote them for a standardized set of environmental parameters, or\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Standard_conditions" title="Standard conditions">\n        standard conditions\n       </a>\n       , including:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        A\n        <a href="/wiki/Temperature" title="Temperature">\n         temperature\n        </a>\n        of 25\xc2\xa0\xc2\xb0C or 298\xc2\xa0K,\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A\n        <a href="/wiki/Pressure" title="Pressure">\n         pressure\n        </a>\n        of one atmosphere (1\xc2\xa0atm or 101.325\xc2\xa0kPa),\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        A\n        <a href="/wiki/Concentration" title="Concentration">\n         concentration\n        </a>\n        of 1.0\xc2\xa0M when the element or compound is present in solution,\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Elements or compounds in their normal physical states, i.e.\n        <a href="/wiki/Standard_state" title="Standard state">\n         standard state\n        </a>\n        .\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       For such standardized values the name of the enthalpy is commonly prefixed with the term\n       <i>\n        standard\n       </i>\n       , e.g.\n       <i>\n        standard enthalpy of formation\n       </i>\n       .\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Chemical properties:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_reaction" title="Enthalpy of reaction">\n         Enthalpy of reaction\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change observed in a constituent of a thermodynamic system when one mole of substance reacts completely.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_formation" title="Enthalpy of formation">\n         Enthalpy of formation\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change observed in a constituent of a thermodynamic system when one mole of a compound is formed from its elementary antecedents.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_combustion" title="Enthalpy of combustion">\n         Enthalpy of combustion\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change observed in a constituent of a thermodynamic system when one mole of a substance burns completely with oxygen.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_hydrogenation" title="Enthalpy of hydrogenation">\n         Enthalpy of hydrogenation\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change observed in a constituent of a thermodynamic system when one mole of an unsaturated compound reacts completely with an excess of hydrogen to form a saturated compound.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_atomization" title="Enthalpy of atomization">\n         Enthalpy of atomization\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change required to atomize one mole of compound completely.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_neutralization" title="Enthalpy of neutralization">\n         Enthalpy of neutralization\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change observed in a constituent of a thermodynamic system when one mole of water is formed when an acid and a base react.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Standard\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_solution" title="Enthalpy of solution">\n         Enthalpy of solution\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change observed in a constituent of a thermodynamic system when one mole of a solute is dissolved completely in an excess of solvent, so that the solution is at infinite dilution.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        Standard enthalpy of\n        <a href="/wiki/Denaturation_(biochemistry)" title="Denaturation (biochemistry)">\n         Denaturation (biochemistry)\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change required to denature one mole of compound.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Hydration_energy" title="Hydration energy">\n         Enthalpy of hydration\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change observed when one mole of gaseous ions are completely dissolved in water forming one mole of aqueous ions.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <p>\n       Physical properties:\n      </p>\n      <ul>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_fusion" title="Enthalpy of fusion">\n         Enthalpy of fusion\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change required to completely change the state of one mole of substance between solid and liquid states.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_vaporization" title="Enthalpy of vaporization">\n         Enthalpy of vaporization\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change required to completely change the state of one mole of substance between liquid and gaseous states.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_sublimation" title="Enthalpy of sublimation">\n         Enthalpy of sublimation\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change required to completely change the state of one mole of substance between solid and gaseous states.\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Lattice_enthalpy" title="Lattice enthalpy">\n         Lattice enthalpy\n        </a>\n        , defined as the energy required to separate one mole of an ionic compound into separated gaseous ions to an infinite distance apart (meaning no force of attraction).\n       </li>\n       <li>\n        <a href="/wiki/Enthalpy_of_mixing" title="Enthalpy of mixing">\n         Enthalpy of mixing\n        </a>\n        , defined as the enthalpy change upon mixing of two (non-reacting) chemical substances.\n       </li>\n      </ul>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Open_systems">\n        Open systems\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Open systems">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       In\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Thermodynamic" title="Thermodynamic">\n        thermodynamic\n       </a>\n       <a href="/wiki/Open_system_(systems_theory)" title="Open system (systems theory)">\n        open systems\n       </a>\n       , matter may flow in and out of the system boundaries. The first law of thermodynamics for open systems states: The increase in the internal energy of a system is equal to the amount of energy added to the system by matter flowing in and by heating, minus the amount lost by matter flowing out and in the form of work done by the system:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               U\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               Q\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                U\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mtext>\n                 in\n                </mtext>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               d\n              </mi>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                U\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mtext>\n                 out\n                </mtext>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               \xce\xb4\n               <!-- \xce\xb4 -->\n              </mi>\n              <mi>\n               W\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle dU=\\delta Q+dU_{\\text{in}}-dU_{\\text{out}}-\\delta W,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle dU=\\delta Q+dU_{\\text{in}}-dU_{\\text{out}}-\\delta W,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/7d68e1a98695ebb3ed8c84c5494ab0a4b64e0d84" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:31.648ex; height:2.676ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where\n       <i>\n        U\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        in\n       </sub>\n       is the average internal energy entering the system, and\n       <i>\n        U\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        out\n       </sub>\n       is the average internal energy leaving the system.\n      </p>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:252px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:First_law_open_system.svg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="257" data-file-width="374" height="172" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/First_law_open_system.svg/250px-First_law_open_system.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/First_law_open_system.svg/375px-First_law_open_system.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/86/First_law_open_system.svg/500px-First_law_open_system.svg.png 2x" width="250"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:First_law_open_system.svg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         During\n         <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steady-state_(chemical_engineering)" title="Steady-state (chemical engineering)">\n          steady, continuous\n         </a>\n         operation, an energy balance applied to an open system equates shaft work performed by the system to heat added plus net enthalpy added\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       The region of space enclosed by the boundaries of the open system is usually called a\n       <a href="/wiki/Control_volume" title="Control volume">\n        control volume\n       </a>\n       , and it may or may not correspond to physical walls. If we choose the shape of the control volume such that all flow in or out occurs perpendicular to its surface, then the flow of matter into the system performs work as if it were a piston of fluid pushing mass into the system, and the system performs work on the flow of matter out as if it were driving a piston of fluid. There are then two types of work performed:\n       <i>\n        flow work\n       </i>\n       described above, which is performed on the fluid (this is also often called\n       <i>\n        pV work\n       </i>\n       ), and\n       <i>\n        shaft work\n       </i>\n       , which may be performed on some mechanical device.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       These two types of work are expressed in the equation\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n
