The term\n       <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n         <i>\n          dV\n         </i>\n         <sub>\n          <i>\n           k\n          </i>\n         </sub>\n        </span>\n        <span class="visualhide">\n         /\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n         <i>\n          dt\n         </i>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       represents the rate of change of the system volume at position\n       <i>\n        k\n       </i>\n       that results in\n       <i>\n        pV\n       </i>\n       power done by the system. The parameter\n       <i>\n        P\n       </i>\n       represents all other forms of power done by the system such as shaft power, but it can also be e.g. electric power produced by an electrical power plant.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Note that the previous expression holds true only if the kinetic energy flow rate is conserved between system inlet and outlet.\n       <sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="margin-left:0.1em; white-space:nowrap;">\n        [\n        <i>\n         <a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Please_clarify" title="Wikipedia:Please clarify">\n          <span title="This new type of energy, kinetic energy, was not mentioned before. Is it part of U? Does it need to be conserved, or just the net flow across boundary be zero? (March 2015)">\n           clarification needed\n          </span>\n         </a>\n        </i>\n        ]\n       </sup>\n       Otherwise, it has to be included in the enthalpy balance. During\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Steady-state_(chemical_engineering)" title="Steady-state (chemical engineering)">\n        steady-state\n       </a>\n       operation of a device (\n       <i>\n        see\n        <a href="/wiki/Turbine" title="Turbine">\n         turbine\n        </a>\n        ,\n        <a href="/wiki/Pump" title="Pump">\n         pump\n        </a>\n        , and\n        <a href="/wiki/Engine" title="Engine">\n         engine\n        </a>\n       </i>\n       ), the average\n       <span class="sfrac nowrap" style="display:inline-block; vertical-align:-0.5em; font-size:85%; text-align:center;">\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em;">\n         <i>\n          dU\n         </i>\n        </span>\n        <span class="visualhide">\n         /\n        </span>\n        <span style="display:block; line-height:1em; margin:0 0.1em; border-top:1px solid;">\n         <i>\n          dt\n         </i>\n        </span>\n       </span>\n       may be set equal to zero. This yields a useful expression for the average\n       <a href="/wiki/Power_(physics)" title="Power (physics)">\n        power\n       </a>\n       generation for these devices in the absence of chemical reactions:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n      <mi>\n                    H\n                   </mi>\n                   <mo>\n                    \xcb\x99\n                    <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                   </mo>\n                  </mover>\n                 </mrow>\n                </mrow>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi>\n                  k\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </msub>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x9f\xa9\n               </mo>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <munder>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x88\x91\n                <!-- \xe2\x88\x91 -->\n               </mo>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mi>\n                 k\n                </mi>\n               </mrow>\n              </munder>\n              <mrow>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x9f\xa8\n               </mo>\n               <msub>\n                <mi>\n                 p\n                </mi>\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi>\n                  k\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </msub>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mfrac>\n                 <mrow>\n                  <mi>\n                   d\n                  </mi>\n                  <msub>\n                   <mi>\n                    V\n                   </mi>\n                   <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                    <mi>\n                     k\n                    </mi>\n                   </mrow>\n                  </msub>\n                 </mrow>\n                 <mrow>\n                  <mi>\n                   d\n                  </mi>\n                  <mi>\n                   t\n                  </mi>\n                 </mrow>\n                </mfrac>\n               </mrow>\n               <mo>\n                \xe2\x9f\xa9\n               </mo>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle P=\\sum _{k}\\left\\langle {\\dot {Q}}_{k}\\right\\rangle +\\sum _{k}\\left\\langle {\\dot {H}}_{k}\\right\\rangle -\\sum _{k}\\left\\langle p_{k}{\\frac {dV_{k}}{dt}}\\right\\rangle ,}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle P=\\sum _{k}\\left\\langle {\\dot {Q}}_{k}\\right\\rangle +\\sum _{k}\\left\\langle {\\dot {H}}_{k}\\right\\rangle -\\sum _{k}\\left\\langle p_{k}{\\frac {dV_{k}}{dt}}\\right\\rangle ,}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/809770d19886b40b43ad3533818f23430a76d7d1" style="vertical-align: -3.171ex; width:45.014ex; height:6.843ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       where the\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Angle_bracket" title="Angle bracket">\n        angle brackets\n       </a>\n       denote time averages. The technical importance of the enthalpy is directly related to its presence in the first law for open systems, as formulated above.\n      </p>\n      <h2>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Diagrams">\n        Diagrams\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Diagrams">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h2>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:502px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="698" data-file-width="1013" height="345" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg/500px-Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg/750px-Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/0/03/Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg/1000px-Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg 2x" width="500"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Ts_diagram_of_N2_02.jpg" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         <i>\n          T\n         </i>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n         <i>\n          s\n         </i>\n         diagram of nitrogen.\n         <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24">\n          <a href="#cite_note-24">\n           [22]\n          </a>\n         </sup>\n         The red curve at the left is the melting curve. The red dome represents the two-phase region with the low-entropy side the saturated liquid and the high-entropy side the saturated gas. The black curves give the\n         <i>\n          T\n         </i>\n         \xe2\x80\x93\n         <i>\n          s\n         </i>\n         relation along isobars. The pressures are indicated in bar. The blue curves are isenthalps (curves of constant enthalpy). The values are indicated in blue in kJ/kg. The specific points\n         <b>\n          a\n         </b>\n         ,\n         <b>\n          b\n         </b>\n         , etc., are treated in the main text.\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       Nowadays the enthalpy values of important substances can be obtained using commercial software. Practically all relevant material properties can be obtained either in tabular or in graphical form. There are many types of diagrams, such as\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x93\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       diagrams, which give the specific enthalpy as function of temperature for various pressures, and\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x93\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       diagrams, which give\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       as function of\n       <i>\n        p\n       </i>\n       for various\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       . One of the most common diagrams is the temperature\xe2\x80\x93specific entropy diagram (\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x93\n       <i>\n        s\n       </i>\n       -diagram). It gives the melting curve and saturated liquid and vapor values together with isobars and isenthalps. These diagrams are powerful tools in the hands of the thermal engineer.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Some_basic_applications">\n        Some basic applications\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Some basic applications">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <p>\n       The points\n       <b>\n        a\n       </b>\n       through\n       <b>\n        h\n       </b>\n       in the figure play a role in the discussion in this section.\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         a\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 300\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 1\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 6.85\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 461\xc2\xa0kJ/kg;\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         b\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 380\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 2\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 6.85\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 530\xc2\xa0kJ/kg;\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         c\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 300\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 200\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 5.16\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 430\xc2\xa0kJ/kg;\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         d\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 270\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 1\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 6.79\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 430\xc2\xa0kJ/kg;\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         e\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 108\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 13\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 3.55\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 100\xc2\xa0kJ/kg (saturated liquid at 13\xc2\xa0bar);\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         f\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 77.2\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 1\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 3.75\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 100\xc2\xa0kJ/kg;\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         g\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 77.2\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 1\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 2.83\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 28\xc2\xa0kJ/kg (saturated liquid at 1\xc2\xa0bar);\n       </dd>\n       <dd>\n        <b>\n         h\n        </b>\n        :\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 77.2\xc2\xa0K,\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 1\xc2\xa0bar,\n        <i>\n         s\n        </i>\n        = 5.41\xc2\xa0kJ/(kg\xc2\xa0K),\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 230\xc2\xa0kJ/kg (saturated gas at 1\xc2\xa0bar);\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Throttling">\n        Throttling\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Throttling">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a href="/wiki/Joule%E2%80%93Thomson_effect" title="Joule\xe2\x80\x93Thomson effect">\n        Joule\xe2\x80\x93Thomson effect\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schematic_of_throttling.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="260" data-file-width="588" height="97" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Schematic_of_throttling.png/220px-Schematic_of_throttling.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Schematic_of_throttling.png/330px-Schematic_of_throttling.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8f/Schematic_of_throttling.png/440px-Schematic_of_throttling.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schematic_of_throttling.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Schematic diagram of a throttling in the steady state. Fluid enters the system (dotted rectangle) at point 1 and leaves it at point 2. The mass flow is\n         <i>\n          \xe1\xb9\x81\n         </i>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       One of the simple applications of the concept of enthalpy is the so-called throttling process, also known as\n       <a href="/wiki/Joule%E2%80%93Thomson_effect" title="Joule\xe2\x80\x93Thomson effect">\n        Joule-Thomson expansion\n       </a>\n       . It concerns a steady adiabatic flow of a fluid through a flow resistance (valve, porous plug, or any other type of flow resistance) as shown in the figure. This process is very important, since it is at the heart of domestic refrigerators, where it is responsible for the temperature drop between ambient temperature and the interior of the refrigerator. It is also the final stage in many types of liquefiers.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       For a steady state flow regime, the enthalpy of the system (dotted rectangle) has to be constant. Hence\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mn>\n               0\n              </mn>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mover>\n                 <mi>\n                  m\n                 </mi>\n                 <mo>\n                  \xcb\x99\n                  <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                 </mo>\n                </mover>\n               </mrow>\n              </mrow>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 1\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mover>\n                 <mi>\n                  m\n                 </mi>\n                 <mo>\n                  \xcb\x99\n                  <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                 </mo>\n                </mover>\n               </mrow>\n              </mrow>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle 0={\\dot {m}}h_{1}-{\\dot {m}}h_{2}.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle 0={\\dot {m}}h_{1}-{\\dot {m}}h_{2}.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/6fdfa430350e7d032effff52266ccd88f6c8d963" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:16.714ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       Since the mass flow is constant, the specific enthalpies at the two sides of the flow resistance are the same:\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 1\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               ,\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle h_{1}=h_{2},}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle h_{1}=h_{2},}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/83eb0493ab74be26fe8e7f6965ded46a6940c691" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:8.588ex; height:2.509ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       that is, the enthalpy per unit mass does not change during the throttling. The consequences of this relation can be demonstrated using the\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x93\n       <i>\n        s\n       </i>\n       diagram above. Point\n       <b>\n        c\n       </b>\n       is at 200\xc2\xa0bar and room temperature (300\xc2\xa0K). A Joule\xe2\x80\x93Thomson expansion from 200\xc2\xa0bar to 1\xc2\xa0bar follows a curve of constant enthalpy of roughly 425\xc2\xa0kJ/kg (not shown in the diagram) lying between the 400 and 450\xc2\xa0kJ/kg isenthalps and ends in point\n       <b>\n        d\n       </b>\n       , which is at a temperature of about 270\xc2\xa0K. Hence the expansion from 200\xc2\xa0bar to 1\xc2\xa0bar cools nitrogen from 300\xc2\xa0K to 270\xc2\xa0K. In the valve, there is a lot of friction, and a lot of entropy is produced, but still the final temperature is below the starting value!\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       Point\n       <b>\n        e\n       </b>\n       is chosen so that it is on the saturated liquid line with\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         h\n        </i>\n        = 100 kJ/kg\n       </span>\n       . It corresponds roughly with\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         p\n        </i>\n        = 13 bar\n       </span>\n       and\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        <i>\n         T\n        </i>\n        = 108 K\n       </span>\n       . Throttling from this point to a pressure of 1\xc2\xa0bar ends in the two-phase region (point\n       <b>\n        f\n       </b>\n       ). This means that a mixture of gas and liquid leaves the throttling valve. Since the enthalpy is an extensive parameter, the enthalpy in\n       <b>\n        f\n       </b>\n       (\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <b>\n         f\n        </b>\n       </sub>\n       ) is equal to the enthalpy in\n       <b>\n        g\n       </b>\n       (\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <b>\n         g\n        </b>\n       </sub>\n       ) multiplied by the liquid fraction in\n       <b>\n        f\n       </b>\n       (\n       <i>\n        x\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <b>\n         f\n        </b>\n       </sub>\n       ) plus the enthalpy in\n       <b>\n        h\n       </b>\n       (\n       <i>\n        h\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <b>\n         h\n        </b>\n       </sub>\n       ) multiplied by the gas fraction in\n       <b>\n        f\n       </b>\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        (1 \xe2\x88\x92\n        <i>\n         x\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         <b>\n          f\n         </b>\n        </sub>\n        )\n       </span>\n       . So\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  f\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                x\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  f\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  g\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               (\n              </mo>\n              <mn>\n               1\n              </mn>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                x\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  f\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo stretchy="false">\n               )\n              </mo>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                 <mi mathvariant="bold">\n                  h\n                 </mi>\n                </mrow>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle h_{\\mathbf {f} }=x_{\\mathbf {f} }h_{\\mathbf {g} }+(1-x_{\\mathbf {f} })h_{\\mathbf {h} }.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle h_{\\mathbf {f} }=x_{\\mathbf {f} }h_{\\mathbf {g} }+(1-x_{\\mathbf {f} })h_{\\mathbf {h} }.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bbdc912a5a88313c4cac5d3893d5d5229a7a4271" style="vertical-align: -1.005ex; width:24.628ex; height:3.009ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       With numbers:\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        100 =\n        <i>\n         x\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         <b>\n          f\n         </b>\n        </sub>\n        \xc3\x97 28 + (1 \xe2\x88\x92\n        <i>\n         x\n        </i>\n        <sub>\n         <b>\n          f\n         </b>\n        </sub>\n        ) \xc3\x97 230\n       </span>\n       , so\n       <i>\n        x\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        <b>\n         f\n        </b>\n       </sub>\n       =\xc2\xa00.64. This means that the mass fraction of the liquid in the liquid\xe2\x80\x93gas mixture that leaves the throttling valve is 64%.\n      </p>\n      <h3>\n       <span class="mw-headline" id="Compressors">\n        Compressors\n       </span>\n       <span class="mw-editsection">\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         [\n        </span>\n        <a href="/w/index.php?title=Enthalpy&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Compressors">\n         edit\n        </a>\n        <span class="mw-editsection-bracket">\n         ]\n        </span>\n       </span>\n      </h3>\n      <div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">\n       Main article:\n       <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Gas_compressor" title="Gas compressor">\n        Gas compressor\n       </a>\n      </div>\n      <div class="thumb tright">\n       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">\n        <a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Schematic_of_compressor.png">\n         <img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="280" data-file-width="566" height="109" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Schematic_of_compressor.png/220px-Schematic_of_compressor.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Schematic_of_compressor.png/330px-Schematic_of_compressor.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/38/Schematic_of_compressor.png/440px-Schematic_of_compressor.png 2x" width="220"/>\n        </a>\n        <div class="thumbcaption">\n         <div class="magnify">\n          <a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Schematic_of_compressor.png" title="Enlarge">\n          </a>\n         </div>\n         Schematic diagram of a compressor in the steady state. Fluid enters the system (dotted rectangle) at point 1 and leaves it at point 2. The mass flow is\n         <i>\n          \xe1\xb9\x81\n         </i>\n         . A power\n         <i>\n          P\n         </i>\n         is applied and a heat flow\n         <i>\n          Q\xcc\x87\n         </i>\n         is released to the surroundings at ambient temperature\n         <i>\n          T\n         </i>\n         <sub>\n          a\n         </sub>\n         .\n        </div>\n       </div>\n      </div>\n      <p>\n       A power\n       <i>\n        P\n       </i>\n       is applied e.g. as electrical power. If the compression is adiabatic, the gas temperature goes up. In the reversible case it would be at constant entropy, which corresponds with a vertical line in the\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x93\n       <i>\n        s\n       </i>\n       diagram. For example, compressing nitrogen from 1 bar (point\n       <b>\n        a\n       </b>\n       ) to 2 bar (point\n       <b>\n        b\n       </b>\n       ) would result in a temperature increase from 300 K to 380 K. In order to let the compressed gas exit at ambient temperature\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       <sub>\n        a\n       </sub>\n       , heat exchange, e.g. by cooling water, is necessary. In the ideal case the compression is isothermal. The average heat flow to the surroundings is\n       <i>\n        Q\xcc\x87\n       </i>\n       . Since the system is in the steady state the first law gives\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math xmlns="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML">\n           <semantics>\n            <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n             <mstyle displaystyle="true" scriptlevel="0">\n              <mn>\n               0\n              </mn>\n              <mo>\n               =\n              </mo>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mover>\n                 <mi>\n                  Q\n                 </mi>\n                 <mo>\n                  \xcb\x99\n                  <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                 </mo>\n                </mover>\n               </mrow>\n              </mrow>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mover>\n                 <mi>\n                  m\n                 </mi>\n                 <mo>\n                  \xcb\x99\n                  <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                 </mo>\n                </mover>\n               </mrow>\n              </mrow>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 1\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               \xe2\x88\x92\n               <!-- \xe2\x88\x92 -->\n              </mo>\n              <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mover>\n                 <mi>\n                  m\n                 </mi>\n                 <mo>\n                  \xcb\x99\n                  <!-- \xcb\x99 -->\n                 </mo>\n                </mover>\n               </mrow>\n              </mrow>\n              <msub>\n               <mi>\n                h\n               </mi>\n               <mrow class="MJX-TeXAtom-ORD">\n                <mn>\n                 2\n                </mn>\n               </mrow>\n              </msub>\n              <mo>\n               +\n              </mo>\n              <mi>\n               P\n              </mi>\n              <mo>\n               .\n              </mo>\n             </mstyle>\n            </mrow>\n            <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">\n             {\\displaystyle 0=-{\\dot {Q}}+{\\dot {m}}h_{1}-{\\dot {m}}h_{2}+P.}\n            </annotation>\n           </semantics>\n          </math>\n         </span>\n         <img alt="{\\displaystyle 0=-{\\dot {Q}}+{\\dot {m}}h_{1}-{\\dot {m}}h_{2}+P.}" aria-hidden="true" class="mwe-math-fallback-image-inline" src="https://wikimedia.org/api/rest_v1/media/math/render/svg/bc4d0abf6ebdbb4bb6d32e939e5428676446902b" style="vertical-align: -0.671ex; width:27.839ex; height:3.176ex;"/>\n        </span>\n       </dd>\n      </dl>\n      <p>\n       The minimal power needed for the compression is realized if the compression is reversible. In that case the\n       <a href="/wiki/Second_law_of_thermodynamics" title="Second law of thermodynamics">\n        second law of thermodynamics\n       </a>\n       for open systems gives\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n          <math With the data, obtained with the\n       <i>\n        T\n       </i>\n       \xe2\x80\x93\n       <i>\n        s\n       </i>\n       diagram, we find a value of\n       <span class="nowrap">\n        (430 \xe2\x88\x92 461) \xe2\x88\x92 300 \xc3\x97 (5.16 \xe2\x88\x92 6.85) =\n       </span>\n       476\xc2\xa0kJ/kg.\n      </p>\n      <p>\n       The relation for the power can be further simplified by writing it as\n      </p>\n      <dl>\n       <dd>\n        <span class="mwe-math-element">\n         <span class="mwe-math-mathml-inline mwe-math-mathml-a11y" style="display: none;">\n
